[2026-02-05T05:30:18Z] Ryan Colaço: A lot of my daily work is centered around this. ↵ The model that came on top in terms of safety in this study (independent, but still preprint..  https://doi.org/10.48550/arXiv.2512.01241) is what the company I work at built... And yet, clinical safety remains an elusive dimension. And, having trained to always be extremely sensitive to how multivarious the clinical process is, I find it crazy that it's so difficult for these folks (and the physicians on their teams) to accept. ↵ When the model was being released, some of us really had to fight internally to make the disclaimer "less optimistic", and it wasn't the simplistic "suits vs scrubs" story...  on the other side of the argument were also other doctor colleagues. ↵ I think, there's a dichotomy to human ideas... And, despite how much we think reading and learning will help us overcome it, one falls on either side, predominantly based on what your lived experiences have been. ↵ It was clear to see that the doctors on the other side were trained in a very "structured" sanitized system, where patientcare was a bit more abstracted, behind the context of time/patient, insurance approvals, rigid duty rosters etc.... On the more cautious side were those with more "raw" experiences (doctors that had worked in international/intersectional settings, ERs, ICUs)... ↵ Not saying either was right or wrong... ↵ But it made it clear to me that our thresholds (as a collective) for this are never going to fully align. ↵ So, then, we should default to the first rule of any form of care : ↵  first, do no harm. ‎<This message was edited>

ISO 9407 is an international standard concerned with how a mass-produced consumer good is dimensioned and labeled, where multiple numerical and symbolic systems coexist and are often confused with one another. ISO 8601 is an international standard that prescribes an unambiguous, strictly ordered way of writing temporal information so that the same sequence of numbers is interpreted identically by humans and machines across borders. [2026-02-06T16:08:09Z] AntNishu: Q17: X is an ancient Indian unit of distance used for over two millennia. Though rendered obsolete after India adopted the metric system in 1956, it survives in language and historical landmarks. Derived from the Sanskrit word meaning a "call", X originally denoted the distance over which a human shout could be clearly heard. Under Akbar, it was standardised as 5,000 Y(aka Mughal Yard), approximately 4.2 km. Remnants of this system endure in the form of X Minars, 30-foot-high brick towers still visible along the old Grand Trunk Road. ↵ ID X, Y

Name Y literally translates to "Big Foot", which is its most defining physical trait, adapted for digging. Shy by nature, it prefers running through undergrowth to flying. ↵ Living in coastal, swamp forests and mangroves, it is best known as a "living incubator."
